Ugh. I don't expect to ever play this again.

RATING: 7
This game is entertaining, but still has a few problems. The combat is pretty fair and the story is nice, but the rules can be unclear about many things. Add on the fact that some heroes are clearly more powerful than others and the fact that two-player mode has each player keeping track of two characters can bog you down even more. The campaign book is interesting and has nice thematic flavor, but it often reuses certain tiles so much that you will often fight with yourself not to skip a few levels to get to the tiles you haven't played on yet.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
My favorite dungeon crawl as it doesn't have the one vs many confrontational element that Descent does.  However this can be a liability as it is tough to 'ease up' when playing with my youngest son.

Edit: Now that I've played the game a few more times, a seven rating definitely seems about right.  My youngest son loves this game, the story elements are fun and the theme is just right.  So game time with the family, that's a win!  However my oldest son has really cooled on the game and doesn't play anymore.  He wants more choices tactically and this game really just boils down to a slugfest.  As the mice have leveled up I think there are some interesting choices with skills (Tilda's Fortify, Maginos' Chain Lightning, Colin's Inspire), so I guess I'm saying I don't completely agree with my son, but I understand his point of view.  There's games out there with better advancement and more variety of maps/monsters/heroes, but they're longer (not good for a young child) and a key point here is they gloss over the story.

I'm very happy I bought this game, it has already provided many hours of entertainment and I'm only halfway through the base game's story.

RATING: 4
This was pitched to me as a light dnd game with amazing components and story. The components and story are amazing, but coming in new to the game and playing with new players the game quickly dismantled into a rulebook read-fest and we weren't able to get through the first quest.

I still really like the game and will definitely work through the campaign, but the number of rules I think put it more on par with medium-weight RPGs. Make sure to read the rulebook, watch a video tutorial, and then a video play through before starting this with a fresh group.

RATING: N/A
I wanted to love this so so much. I painted up all the wonderful models before I played it and got so very excited about getting it to the table. Yes it's adorable and very rich in backstory, but the gameplay is just not there. Very few tiles have enough obstacles that prevent you from reaching any enemy, so the entire game feels like throwing dice until you win, or until the game just fizzles out and you have to start again.

Not enough decision making, not enough strategy. Roll the dice, hope for the best and enjoy the story.

RATING: 6
Συνεργατικό dungeon crawler παιχνίδι με όμορφες μινιατούρες και ενδιαφέρον θέμα. Το παιχνίδι στηρίζεται πολύ στο έντονο θέμα του το οποίο και υποστηρίζει με όμορφες ιστορίες κατά την διάρκεια της campaign. Μιλάμε για σελίδες κείμενο. Οι μηχανισμοί είναι πολύ απλοί και υπάρχει μπόλικο ζάρι κυρίως στις μάχες αλλά και λίγο στη κίνηση των χαρακτήρων. Το αποτέλεσμα είναι λίγες τακτικές αποφάσεις για τους παίκτες.

Οι εχθροί κινούνται από μόνοι τους με συγκεκριμένη λογική. Οι melee εχθροί πάνε και βαράνε τον πλησιέστερο ήρωα ενώ οι ranged εχθροί βαράνε από μακριά. Θα ήθελα μεγαλύτερη ποικιλία εδώ. Υπάρχει πληθώρα από equipments αλλά και skills που μπορείς να μάθεις κάνοντας level-up. To παιχνίδι χρησιμοποιεί το τυρί σαν mana για τα skills και σαν XP για level up. Διαλέγεις πως θα το χρησιμοποιήσεις.

Πολύ όμορφο και παραμυθένιο το artwork και γενικότερα τα components. Το Story είναι που κρατάει το ενδιαφέρον σου κατά την διάρκεια της campaign. Θα ήθελα να είχε πιο πολλές τακτικές επιλογές. Επίσης οι 2 πρώτες αποστολές μας φάνηκαν πολύ εύκολες. Ελπίζω να δυσκολεύει μετά γιατί ως γνωστόν συνεργατικό και εύκολο καταντά βαρετό γρήγορα.

Το παιχνίδι δείχνει να απευθύνεται περισσότερο σε οικογένειες με παιδιά, χωρίς αυτό να σημαίνει πως δεν μπορούν να το απολαύσουν και καμένοι gamers.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Rating based on 1 play:

I liked it.  Initially it took us quite a while to get into the rules - lost of flicking back and forwards and loads of questions that needed clarifying.

What I did love was the artwork - gorgeous.  Them theme is certainly more family friendly than a dungeon crawl.  The minis are lovely but I;d really love to see more variety in the types of baddies (I presume more will follow in expansions).  

Combat is as simple as can be - lovely.  Most actions and moves are intuitive.  The chapter progression is handled incredibly well, changing initiative was clever and the cheese, being both good and bad is an inspired mechanism that both progresses the story progression and is used for character development.

Once we got past the rule clarifications and into the game, the turns flew by and just when we thought the game was too easy, things ramped-up.  Initially, we concentrated more on gameplay and ignored the story to an extent, but I'm keen to reveal it further and to play again.

RATING: 9
Positive: It is easy enough to play with non-gamers and/or children.
Negative: It is about as interesting as a game that is easy enough to play with non-gamers and/or children can be.

Positive: Nice miniatures.
Negative: Nice miniatures--at the expense of having interesting game play.

EDIT; Now that I have played other dungeon crawlers and have something to actually compare this game to, it's actually quite charming.  The gameplay is very smooth and intuitive, and the rules are surprising uncomplicated.  The story line is a bit silly (though to be honest, all dungeon crawl storylines are silly--that's what makes them fun).  I actually appreciate the consistency of the storytelling--here you will find no random mashup of Tolkein, Greco-Roman Mythology, Norse Mythology, Christian supernatural beings, and generic D and D shenanigans. 

All in all, this turned out to be one of my favorite guilty-pleasures to play solo.  But it is easy enough that I can teach it to gamers and non-gamers alike.

RATING: 9
We love this game. A dungeon crawl with a good theme and a delightful story to back it up. The miniatures in this game were so cool it inspired my wife to take up the hobby of painting minis. Some of the rules can become a bit fiddly and bog down the game play but those incidents are few and far between. The biggest problem we have with it is that "cheese wheel." It can fill up so fast thanks to enemies rolling cheese that we've had to house rule that after each board (both sides) are completed we clear the cheese wheel otherwise we never finish. I'm sure some of you will cry foul but this is the only game we own where we are enjoying playing through the story more than the actual game play.

RATING: 6.5
I want to like this game so much.  It wants to be Redwall - the board game.  The theme and the production of the game are top notch.  But somehow the game struggles to rise to expectations.  The first issue I have is that its a tad fiddly.  There are cards for this and that and those and getting it set up seems to take a long time.  The rules - while well written - seem to find a way of being forgotten between sessions.  When do I add cheese to the clock?  What does it take to get out of the water?  Isn't there something special about that darn Brodie?  These could be dismissed as not having focused and knowledgeable gamers playing.  But I think the biggest drawback to this game is that it is so wickedly hard!  Perhaps we've just always gotten the rules somehow wrong.  Or we are bad at setting up characters, or have really bad luck... but winning even the first scenario has proven ard enough that multiple attempts have ended in TPKs (total party kills).  That shouldn't happen in the 1st scenario.  That's just too discouraging for younger family members that really, really want to like the game too.

RATING: 7
Egy nagyon jó hangulatú játék lenne, talán csak az első parti szokásos kis félreértései miatt nem volt átütő élmény. Egyébként szerintem egy egyszerűsített, kevésbé sötét Odalent-szerűség, ami így családibb játék is annál. A pályaépítés egyszerű, az alapmechanizmusok is pofonegyszerűek (támadás, mozgás), kevés fajta akció van, és szinte mindig egyértelmű, hogy mit kell csinálni (ha van mód támadásra akkor szinte mindig azt kell tenni), de azért mint az ilyen jellegű játékoknál általában, itt is megtaláljuk a sok kivételt. Emellett sajnos néhány szabály azért nem volt egyértelmű, pl. a patkányok és csótányok esetében az életszám megtévesztően van jelölve... A keresés paklit kicsit haszontalannak éreztem, a sajtozás jó ötlet és tematikus. Jó ötlet az összetűzés sorrend is, és hogy bizonyos képességek ehhez kapcsolódnak (pl. patkányoknál, Filchnél). A történettábla is nagyon tetszik. És a játék közbeni sztori mesélés is, bár ez alapból nem áll hozzám közel, de rásegít a hangulatra.
Összességében egy hangulatos jó kis kooperatív kalandjáték, helyenként nem túl egzakt szabállyal, és határesetként akár kisebb gyerekekkel is játszható, bár felnőtteknek se könnyű.

RATING: 6.5
Mice and Mystics is a fairly typical dungeon crawler, with surprisingly easy rules (I can't wait to play it with my daughters when they grow up) and a fresh theme, very similar to Mouse Guard graphic novel.
The better part of the game lies in the story: the game is designed to be played as a campaign by the same group of players, and there's plenty of stuff to read aloud to live a great experience together.
The slightly disappointing part is the decision making: you move and do things (or vice versa) and everything is pretty simple to figure out. It is family and non-gamer friendly, but I hope that future scenarios are a little more challenging.
Anyway, I'd recommend it for groups who want to live the adventure, especially if they include kids!

RATING: 8
Initial Impression: This is a family friendly dungeon crawler game. The theme and story are instantly compelling and the rules are easy to grasp. The game flows really well after the initial few turns. The characters come alive with retained skills, equipment, and background story. The minis scream to be painted. I'm hoping to see many more expansions to the game in the near future. 

10 Plays: My son and I are enjoying the game together. He's been interested in the character progression and I've been hooked on the story. We've already agreed to buy and play all the forseeable expansions. Although the gameplay is light, we actually find that a positive in that the rules don't get in the way of the great narrative. I've painted the minis and created a custom insert to make setup/breakdown alot quicker.

20 Plays: My son and I stalled at the beginning of Chapter 8 and I eventually lost him to the lure of video games. As such, I've restarted the story from the beginning. As it had been almost a year since our last session, I'm rediscovering the magic of the story (yeah, my memory is terrible). This time I've purposely chosen characters in order to create an odd mix of personalities/abilities in order to crank up the difficulty and I have to say that it's been working. For myself, this is an enjoyable game even the second time around.

40 Plays: After watching me struggle through some of the later chapters, my son was once again drawn into the story and helped me complete the adventure. The final chapters are VERY interesting and I highly recommend sticking it out through to the end of the story. The character progression is wonderful and we truly enjoyed the story. Although I'll be jumping into Heart of Glorm by myself, my son has asked me to let him know when we can tackle Downwood Tales together.

RATING: 7
I love the idea of this game.  Playing a game that is part of a story is a lot if fun.  It is not a game you play for the challenge.  The number of decisions you make are fairly limited and usually obvious.  That's not to say the game is easy though - we got trounced on our first two attempts through the first chapter.  My only complaint is that character/minion movement kind of stinks - most of the time you can get most of the way across the tile in a single turn.  It doesn't allow for much strategy in terms of positioning, and all of the mice/minions tend to end up in a clump.  But really the reason we play this game is for the story, and that part is great.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
Dungeon Crawler where you play as a group of enchanted mice.

Tiptoe through the castle's chambers or scurry through the tunnels beneath the ancient stone walls.
Fight off evil rat-guardsmen, creepy spiders, small roaches or giant centipedes to discover the secret of the malicious Vanestra. 

Choose between the usual archetypes: Such as warrior, archer, mage, healer or rogue and set up a group of adventurer for each session.
Your party fights through eleven colorful illustrated and warmly written chapters - using gear that can be found in the chambers and tunnels within the castle.
Rely on abilities that can be obtained by spending cheese (kind of the usual experience points) and last but not least hope for the cheese to be rolled on your turn and not during the enemies.

If you like a “light” dungeon crawler or are a fan of classic pen&paper adventures, this might just be the boardgame you have been waiting for.

Chapter takes around 60 min to finish.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Although on the simple side, M&M (as Rio calls it) plays well and is a whole lot of fun. The components are nice, the minis painted up nicely, and the most important thing is that Rio is really enjoying this game...he finally seems to be back in a boardgaming mood.

5/5/13: I'm changing my rating to a 7. The game is too much about preventing cheese going on to the cheese wheel. There is almost no danger that the mice get killed (captured). Every time we loose, it is because the minions rolled lots of cheese, bringing the game to an end before we could complete the objectives. Therefore we are just looking for ways to slow the cheese wheel, like attacking primarily with Filch and Lily.

Currently in our campaign game we are as follows:

Maginos:
chain lightning
warding staff

Filch:
Find, Energry Rush, Dodge
Ring of Cat Strength

Lily:
Preemptive Shot, Accurate Shot
Mystic Tomb

Tilda:
Cure, First Aid
Toothpick

Collin:
Battle Leader, Give Order
Mystic Blade

Nez:
Battle Squeak, Set Trap
Walnut Shell Breastplate

9/8/13: We tried this again with the following house rules designed to make the game more about surviving combat and less about preventing cheese going on the cheese wheel:
- Filling the Cheese Wheel does not advance the chapter if it causes a surge;
- Every foe has +1 hearts.
After playtesting this we decided it wasn't working. Extra hearts for minions means extended play time, so we dropped that. Not advancing the chapter with a surge was too easy, so we dropped that as well. So we had a long game that was too easy...not good.

9/10/13:
We tried playing with cheese rolled on minion's dice is ignored, and any mice wounds puts 2 cheese on the cheese wheel. This was pretty tough, but it is nice in that defending minions don't put cheese on wheel...we like that!

9/11/13: New house rules seem almost right!
Minion dice do not add to cheese wheel.
Every mouse wound puts one cheese on the cheese wheel. This is a little too easy. But we like the feel. The game plays faster because if you auto-kill a minion, you don't have to roll for cheese. There are a few other tweaks necessary. For example, greedy roaches now steal 2 cheese, rather than stealing cheese and putting it on the cheese wheel (they still only do 1 damage, and if a mouse has only one cheese, they just steal one). So we should just be able to add a little something to make it a little tougher and I think we've got a better game!

9/14: So these new house rules are working pretty well in terms of the feel of the game, but now the game is too easy. We are going to make the opponents harder.
Spider: can make either a melee or ranged attack.
Roach: is granted a "Charge" ability. If after moving it is unable to make a melee attack, it can use one of its attack dice to make another movement roll. It continues doing this until it can make an attack or it runs out of dice.
Roaches and Rats: Every time roaches and rats spawn, designate one figure as a "Boss". Its stats are all at +1, including hearts.
These house rules are holding up pretty well, if a little on the easy side...

Currently in our campaign game we are on chapter 5 and equiped as follows:

Maginos:
chain lightning, meeps, invisibility
Lucky Skullcap

Filch:
Energry Rush
Spear

Lily:
Preemptive Shot, Accurate Shot, power shot, aimed shot, keen eye.
Accurate Bow

Tilda:
First Aid
Button Shield

Collin:
Inspire
Thimble Helm

Nez:
Battle Squeak, Set Trap
Walnut Shell Breastplate
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
I used to love Mice and Mystics because of its theme: now, thirty games later, the spell has ended (along with the campaign). With the right group - mainly kids or non-gamers - it still works as a gateway game and might even be a hit: but in the end it’s too repetitive to keep its allure on gamers of any other kind. 

Actually all you can do over and over is fighting, finding new ways to optimize your party’s skills and searching for items you most likely won’t be allowed to take into the next scenario: in the end it’s just Heroquest with cheese and a cute wrapping.

The worse is, with so many good cooperatives around that never play the same I can’t see Mice and Mystics played too often by my regular group: rather, as soon as we’re over with Glorm as well I think it’ll be buried on the shelf with the other well-meaning games that we never play.

RATING: 10
This is a fantastic adventure and exploration story game. There is never a time that I don't want this to hit the table. The characters feel different, the story is incredibly engaging, and the game play is simple, elegant and enjoyable. The minis in this game are fun to paint and make the experience even better having them come to life with color. I would say the best thing about this game is that it is a fantastic way to introduce people to adventure games because it's approachable, but also has lots of depth and keeps even seasoned gamers engaged. It's a great way to get into miniature painting because the fantastic character sheets that come with each mini give players a guideline for painting and picking colors. All around this is an incredible game, I can't recommend it enough.

RATING: 6
Decent story-driven 'dungeon crawl'. I've only gotten through the first chapter (on the third attempt, but first time with my daughter who is a great roller), and I can see a couple of problems. The main being it seems like we've seen the whole game already. We've fought and beaten all the miniatures in the game, just not the bosses. Sure there will be new map tiles, but no real satisfying level up achievements (just new abilities of which we've already picked the best), and no escalating power for minions, again just the bosses. Second main issue for me seems to be limited strategic choices. So far we basically just attack the closest foe and hope for good rolls, really with a choice on whether to spend a cheese to use a power or not. Hopefully more opens up. 

My daughter likes the story so far so that's good, the production values are great (I've painted the minis), and the base mechanics are good.  But I do wonder if we'll get through the whole campaign.

RATING: 7
Mice and Mystics is probably the best storytelling game I've played. And, I didn't realize before playing how important and embedded the "choose-your-own-adventure" storytelling nature is to the game experience. It's got familiar dungeon crawl mechanics, but with a wonderful theme/flavor and a very approachable system. We were up and running in no time with our first chapter.

This is light years ahead of something like Tales of Arabian Nights, which is all "story" but with nothing actually backing that veneer up in gameplay.

RATING: 7.5

I can easily see this as the kind of game that could convert novices to the genre into fans - especially children, for whom the game is tailor made.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Overall rating 6. Rating for a group of adult gamers 4. Solo rating 6. Rating as a family game 8. I find the game a dull repetitive affair with very little meaningful decision-making. However, it is great game to play with kids. The strongest aspect of the game is theme and looks: the component quality is very high, art is superb etc (rating +2). Plus there are some nice ideas, such as  as spaces corresponding to the objects in the rooms, some items, such as fork catapult etc. (rating +1). I am neutral in regard to several aspects of the game. For instance, it is great to have the campaign woven into a story but the story is not that good. Try to translate it - I have to because my kids do not speak English – and you will see how empty it occasionally is. Sometimes I also have to skip paragraphs because they do not fit the actual game session: often you have a specific mouse speaking of things which are specific to him/her but the mouse may not be in this particular game. Some aspects of the game are bad: the rules overhead is ridiculous considering how light the game is (rating -2);  the game is also too shallow with basically no meaningful decision-making. (rating -2) the mouse abilities are not balanced (rating -1) and the movement die slows the game down and can be frustrating (rating -1). To sum up. It is a nice looking game but too light and repetitive for serious gamers. It is a great family game, though, if one of the parents is willing to invest in learning the rules and takes the responsibility for running the sessions filling in the gaps and making things up to make it more entertaining for the kids.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
A very charming, Redwall style story driven, co-op modular adventure game. I LOVE this game. The rule book is set up in a clever manner, making it like a story book in nature. The book explains the basic premise of a Prince and his friends who are turned into Mice by an evil sorceress. She has made the Prince's father, the King, ill and intends to kill him so she can take his throne with the Prince and his friends out of the way.

It's up to you and your friends to find you way through the castle, fending off anthropomorphic rats, spoopy spiders ; roaches ; and centipedes, as well as avoiding the sorceress' nasty cat. Find equipment, gain character abilities, etc. The game's scenarios each cover a different 'chapter' of the book and some even had side objectives you can complete as well. 

I highly recommend this game for players new to tabletop due to it's very light on mechanic nature and rich story telling. Combat is pretty basic and easy to grasp, the components are beautiful (I had the stock tan minis painted by a good friend to liven up the board even more) and the story is genuinely interesting and charmingly written.

Wonderful, wonderful game.

RATING: 8
[b]Miniature Market - Christmas 2014[/b] 
This is the closest game I have to an Ameritrash game.  I really love the story lines in this game.  The game-play is fun, but the timer mechanism can make it difficult to be able to complete side quests.  There are a lot of variability in this game that makes the replay-ability interesting.

One downside was getting the treachery card that cause all the hordes of bad guys to come at us at once.  We all got knocked out one by one and ended up not being able to win the game because we all got captured.

Another confusing rule was ending the round knocking out the minions causes the medium bad guy to appear.  I did read that an alternate rule would make an exception to this if it were the last player in turn order who took out the last minion would get an extra round to escape the room.

RATING: 6
German edition, at least, has not good quality components. Tiles, cards and character sheets are low quality (you will need sleeves from the first play for the cards) and printing is not so good as you can expect from a standard published game.

It's very dissapointing for me each time I open the box. Components don't fit. There is no custom nest for the tiles, for example, so they move against the sides of the box and so on. I had to add some zip bags for the tokens to keep a minimum order.

The game itself seems ok and it's amusing for little kids. For grown up people... I'm not sure. There are many holes in the rules to take it as a serious game. It reminds me of Heroquest with the fairy theme around, and that's fine, but I expect a corrected edition and some community fixes to the rules soon :D

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Love the concept[*], love the artwork / bits / production, love some of the details. (Cheese wedges as a clock. Time pressure even between encounters. Leveling up / special abilities. The flipping boards for up/down.)

But... holy crud, the dice-rolling. It's not the raw quantity - I play RPGs with lots of dice-rolling - so it's either the swinginess (few dice rolled at once = high variance) or that it feels kind of like a slogfest (doing a lot more rolling-of-dice than anything else). The positioning was interesting when it came up, but at least with melee foes it seemed like past a certain point it was only relevant insofar as you could tweak who was getting attacked how often.

Also, I'm kind of irritated / disappointed at the way the story uses certain gender tropes. In the base game and scenario book, all of the virtuous/powerful NPC good-guys are male, and the villains are an evil sorceress and her conniving daughter. There are 6 playable PCs, 2 of whom are female: one is a healer, and the other you can't play until you've rescued her. Obviously, this isn't enough to bother everyone, but it bothers me.

* = Though I'd have liked it even more if it weren't about humans-turned-mice, but always-mice, a la Mouse Guard.

RATING: 6
Components: Top notch production quality in all respects. Lots of delicious details in the artwork that greatly enhances the theme.

Experience: Lots of fiddly rules, but otherwise entertaining. I like being lead through the narrative. Our diminutive stature helps to make the story even more immersive and fun. There aren't huge numbers of interesting decisions to be made on a turn, and there is a ton of dice rolling, but I enjoy seeing how the conflicts pan out.

After two plays, I'm not seeing how my decisions are greatly affecting the outcome. After getting creamed in the second game, much worse than in our naive first game, I feel at the whim of the game's luck.

Last Played: 2013-06-24
Eagerness to Play Again: Within a year

RATING: 6.5
(borrowed from the library)
Amazing graphic design and production values. I can see younger players diving right into the world of Mice and Mystics and having a great time.

For adult gamers however there's simply not enough gameplay choices or strategic/tactical decisions to be made. This game is all about story and theme. Playing the game is mostly about throwing dice and because of this we ran into situations where the mice were constantly captured because of repeated bad luck with the dice (this can result to both getting beaten up in battle and the cheese clock constantly being filled and spawning new enemies).

There's clearly so much love and effort put into this game that it's a pity there's not enough depth for more mature gamers.

RATING: N/A
Mice and Mystics (4) seconda partita per me e prima per gli altri. sbagliamo ad interpretare i simboli sui dadi per la prima parte della partita (cosa che poi ha determinato la sconfitta- colpa mia che sono una lettrice di regolamenti davvero pessima!!) ma quando ci accorgiamo che spada/scudo vale come risultato per l'attacco  ragni, blatte e millepiedi cominciano a morire a manciate!  
gran bel gioco e non vedo l'ora di giocarci ancora!!! 
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Ieri sera lunghissima, emozionante, frustrante, coinvolgente, divertente, sorprendente partita a Mice and Mystics, edizione italiana appena comprata. i topi sono sconfitti in cucina mentre tentano di battere il malefico gatto Brodie. Ma non è il felino il responsabile della disfatta, bensì un troppo entusiasta topo mago, Maginos, che con un'esplosione ha la meglio, sì sul gatto, ma anche sui suoi compagni!!  
Il gioco è bello, bello, bello! componenti da paura, grafica eccellente, ambientazione riuscita, sentita, rispettata... manciate e manciate di dadi da lanciare, carte da pescare, formaggio che attiva abilità, ratti, blatte e millepiedi da affrontare... BELLOOOOO!
-------------------------------------------------------------------------

RATING: 5
Late to the party on M+M, but I had high hopes.   Have to say I was pretty disappointed.   The production is nice, the miniatures are very well done, the books are nice (looking), but the system itself is rather basic and dull.  The rules leave a lot of holes for such a simple game, which is frustrating.   The story elements are the best thing here, because the actual game mechanics are boring and very repetitive.   I think this would have been a big hit about 6 years ago when my kids were younger.   For an entry-level dungeon crawler with a good (but derivative) narrative arc, this might be a great selection, but I don't see it getting much play for me, personally.  The right audience will love this.  But I'd much rather play Talisman, Space Hulk, or DungeonQuest.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Cute, very thematic, and sure looks nice, but it's a kids game only IMO. The game gets kudos for being very thematic and driving a scenario-based story; it's probably a great option for young kids, though I'd probably still nerf the knockouts. Unfortunately, the gameplay is tedious and dull to the point where you're just throwing dice with a minimal amount of decisions. 

The biggest drawback to me is how unforgiving the game is. If you roll poorly, there's very little chance you're going to recover. If a character gets knocked out and you're a man down, you're pretty much done. There should be ways to overcome some missed shots/lost characters, otherwise one bad turn and the attrition makes playing any further a moot point, and then you have restart the whole chapter. I would recommend that knocked out characters lose a turn then come back; sheesh, even Descent gives you this much cushion.

RATING: 4
[b]Gave Away[/b]
see previous comments below.

[b]previous comment:[/b]

I got Mice and Mystics in a trade a long time ago, played the first mission and quickly put it away.  Recently, I've been going through my collection, identifying games that don't get played and should be considered for trade or donation.  I decided to play one more mission, just to make sure I wasn't missing anything, before it went on the chopping block.

I got through setup and started reading the mission rules, got bored, and put the game away.  The mechanics are the easiest of easy roll-and-see-if-I-hit silliness, and the minimal character progression and variety from equipment options is nowhere near enough to rekindle my interest in what are completely uninspiring mechanics.  The story of the game is quite good, and I think I might just read the story bits out of the rule book before getting rid of it, but the actual gameplay is utterly unengaging.  At bare minimum, the different rules for each room during a mission should be on separate cards which can be placed next to that room for easy reference.  Playing a game with a rule book sitting in my lap is just not interesting to me.

I am typically pretty hesitant to rate a game until I've played many times, but the fact that this game manages to mesh extremely simple gameplay with way-too-complicated rules for that gameplay means I can be pretty confident that it lands in the "could be convinced to play (with someone who has the rules memorized) I guess" category.

This is a game that I could see being wonderful to play with children, with the adult acting as a sort of DM.  Since I don't have kids, if I have to sit there with a rule book in my lap, DMing my own on-rails adventure story, I'd much rather just DM a game of D&D and have some actual interesting decisions to make.

RATING: 3
2017-02-20: I knew this would be a 'dumbed down' version of dungeoncrawl but it has a lot of people raving about it so I had some hopes about this game. 

I think my reaction to this shows how much I've 'grown' as a gamer since the 90s when this would probably have been OK. I just found it stupidly repetitive! That there is so few different monsters in the box definitely doesn't help either.

Every part of the scenario went:
Flip a board. Add enemies. Run up to them and roll a gazillion dice. Repeat. Repeat. Repeat.
There is some minimal strategy to where to stand and when to kill/run in regards to the timing of the cheese-wheel, but it is abysmal.
It is just, mostly, rolling dice and doing the quite obvious choices.
I understand the theme and mechanics are meant to allow kids to join in and play the game but boy. . . . what kid can stand these dragged out 2-3 hours game of rolling rolling rolling?
Very disappointed. I might play through the game solo just to have done it, but I'm really not sure it is worth it.
50usd down the drain. sigh. . . 

And I thought the rules were actually quite hard to follow. The rules are there for the most part, it is just a bad 'flow' in the structure of the rules.

initial rating = 3 (sooooo repetitive!)

RATING: 8.5
A medium-light heavily thematic game that has the appeal of a dungeon crawl all while maintaining a whimsical theme of mice warriors.

The "AI" of the game presents challenging decisions to make but keeps the game at a level that it can still be defeated - and it can still defeat you (none of that overbearing "AI" victory nonsense we find in games like Arkham Horror.

If you need a break from more intense games that are trying on any veteran game player's stamina and patience, Mice and Mystics is a fantastic game to enter into the realm of mice-dom and slay you some vermin!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Sort of a child-friendly dungeon crawler. Think of Descent but add a cute backstory and cut down on rules (and, incidentally, largely on decisions). Despite these changes to become more accessible the game is still somewhat fiddly in parts, and the rules have about as many holes as the featured cheese. Due to the lack of notable decisions the game quickly becomes somewhat repetitive once the story loses a bit of its luster (the standard play sequence being: enter new room, kill all enemies, advance to next room). It also seems like the balance can tilt heavily either way because of how the game deals with random encounters.

Mice and Mystics is likely a good choice with children, going on an adventure and experiencing a fairy tale together. For (somewhat) grown-up dungeon crawlers, however, the game offers little excitement and cannot truly challenge the veterans.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
There are some very good ideas in this game - I love the double-sided boards and the initiative system. However in play the randomness of the dice overwhelm everything else, and I found the combat fiddly and not much fun. Since that's mostly what you do in the game, I wasn't so impressed.

In my second play I was doing very well in the first scenario and went to the kitchen. The roaches rolled a lot of cheese, the cat appeared, and killed us all. Not very interesting. I think I'm done with this game. I'm glad I didn't buy it.

FWIW I thought the rules were perfectly adequate. Several people have mentioned doing away with the defence rolls - I agree entirely. Way too boring.

RATING: 7
Perfect for my young kids, and perhaps a gateway to other fantasy games like Descent and HeroQuest.  Kudos to Plaid Hat Games for designing a relatively simple dungeon crawler with a very immersive storyline.  Components are also top notch.  The rulebook does not go into enough detail to satisfy many situations that arise during gameplay, so I recommend improvising to not slow down gameplay.  There is a lot of dice rolling in the game (i.e. for movement), and it's disappointing when a series of bad dice rolls ruins your chance of winning a chapter.  Overall, it's not a perfect, but this is a fun and cute fantasy game that the family enjoys.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
It's "fiddly." It does a good job of creating a dungeon crawl, and after you've played a few of the scenarios you realize the game is ripe with potential at creating your own adventures. BUT- the rules get in the way, and the  fantasy story that comes with the game is, I'm sorry to say, not well written. It honestly could have used a good copy editor.
And there's the rub for me.

This game is supposed to be ALL ABOUT THE STORY and for this part to fall short really takes the whole game down several notches for me. 
As a writer, it annoys me greatly.

Yes, it's supposed to be a "children's story." But,two  "ly" adverbs in the opening sentence, trite character behaviors based on class, and uninspired dialogue make it read more like a junior-high schooler's attempt at Secret of NIMH fan ficton.
Read by and enjoyed by a child, FINE.
Written by a child? NO.
With a few revisions and a little more structure, the story could have been good enough, and it would have helped the game immensely in my opinion.

On it's own, Mice and Mystics is a fine dungeon crawl, and a great effort from Plaid Hat Games. The components are top notch, the included figures have great detail, and it can be infinitely repayable. But there are other games out there that do this better: Descent: Journeys in the Dark, Super Dungeon Explore, Mage Knight, even Munchkin.

I don't know why you'd have to have this in your collection. I bought it because of the rave reviews I read including one on Drake's Flames.
Sorry, Matt. You were off on this one. 
Artistically, however, it looks great on the shelf, which in my house, is were is stays most of the time.

RATING: 5
I LOVE the mice pawns (and I even bought the Lily doll) but I really don't like the way this game treats rats. Real rats are intelligent, social animals, and they're friendly and loving pets. Do we have to trash one rodent to be allowed to appreciate another?

Though, given Redwall (aka "Racism for Beginners") seems to be a major inspiration, I guess I shouldn't be too surprised.

BGG's rating scale is based on how much and how often you want to play the game in question, not how well-designed you think the mechanics are. A game that's well-designed but has themes that make you less interested in playing it should be given a lower score. In the end it all averages out.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.6
The components and the story are great. We are playing as a campaign and I must say our characters are getting a bit overpowered as we approach the end of the main story book. We have been leveling up along the way and have managed to obtain some very nice equipment. On our second play through I am going to suggest that if a character dies he/she starts from scratch again. I am not quite sure about replay ability yet as this is our first time through, but I think the base game is good for at least two campaigns which in our case would be 30-40 plays (with the same group). Of course this type of game will play differently with different groups, so your mileage may vary depending on the situation. 

There is a bit of randomness with the dice of course, but with careful item and ability selection this can be mitigated somewhat. This game plays well with my adult game group as well as with my teenage children, so it has that going for it as well. Overall I highly recommend.

After 30 plays I find my self wanting to play this more than I did when I started. The characters and the story really grow on you. 

Blown past 40 plays and could easily go through the campaign a few more times. As it is we moved on to Glorm and absolutely love it as well. Game is like a fine wine, my rating keeps ticking up over time.

RATING: 7
Great fun game, easy to play and takes little to get used to. Takes a while on the first play through but once the basics are learned it massively speeds up and becomes much more enjoyable. Though the games best feature is the story/campaign feeling to playing your characters, seeing them level up and gain cool loot. this can be carried on to the next chapters and so forth. works very well. though surprised the game didn't come with a cheat sheet of how to keep track of these. we made our own!
Game does however need more enemies, as fighting the same ones over and over became a bit tedious. Needed that little bit more variety.

Recommended fr younger players and or families into D&D style questing.
Though also fun for hardcore guy, I imagine they will get bored quicker as the game goes on due to the repetitive nature.

D.A

Esta es una de mis asignaturas pendientes con el Sr. Vega. 

Es un dungeon crawler, pero como nota definitoria, es que los protagonistas son... ratones. y toda la historia es consecuente a ello. 

vamos, que un poco es como coger el concepto de aquella pelicula de disney "basil, the great mouse detective" (ratones antropomorfos que hacen lo equivalente a seres humanos) pero en un juego de mesa de mazmorreo. me encanta. xD

el problema es que "la unica manera de jugarlo es jugando la campaña entera", y claro. como esta el patio, como para montar una campaña. o_O

una curiosidad: aunque aqui en la lista y practicamente todo el mundo lo conoce por su titulo original en ingles, el juego en españa se publico con el titulo traducido "De Ratones y Magia". 

en fin. "pendiente de ver mesa", y probablemente seguira pendiente en 2032. :/

RATING: 8
A dungeoncrawler game that you can play with kids, with nongamers, and with gamers alike!

This game focuses on creating a thematic atmosphere instead of trying to be a perfect combat simulator. As a result, some rules feel unpolished and/or gamey, but this allows to have a fluid game with great atmosphere, quite good IA for the enemies and a few tense moments. And it doesn't need a DM!

It's great to have a game that does not try to be another Descent. Mice and Mystics can coexist with Descent in your collection.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Mice and Mystics is a great game for those looking into an introductory dungeon crawl with a really charming story. However, for those looking for a meatier game with deep character progression and a branching, complex story may feel underwhelmed by what M & M offers. 

I fall right in between. To me, Gloomhaven is the ideal Dungeon-Crawl/Fantasy/RPG/Character Progression BOARDGAME(I have to capitalize this, cause I know D&D exists) available on the market today, but it is quite an involved game. But its mechanisms and originality is why I think it's great, and games like Mice and Mystics or Descent or many other dungeon crawls just fall flat. 

I'll say it, I am not a fan of dice resolution for combat/blocking/movement etc. in longer games. Black Plague is sort of an exception, because it's not a serious game, heavy game. Chuck some dice, and kill zombies. However if you hate rolling dice constantly, you will hate M&M. You roll when you move, attack, defend , when enemies defend, resolving certain special scenario actions etc. M&M has too much dice rolling for my enjoyment. What's worse you can get stuck in a scenario because you can't kill this one annoying rat hindering progress because he keeps blocking your attacks. 

Listen I enjoy games with dice rolling, but they always need some sort of mitigation on the luck factor( like Roll for the Galaxy has), and my plays of this there was very little to none. Plus I didn't feel like my character was progressing/leveling up etc. 

But where I will give Mice and Mystics its due is in the story it tells, and the ease of play, for the most part. It is a good family game, that younger children can enjoy, as well as parents or young adults. For me, it's a bit simplistic for the style of game it is. I enjoy stupid simple games like Dixit, Bang! the dice game, Ticket to ride, etc. but I want more from my dungeon crawls.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
For all the mousey thematic dressing (which is very well done), this is a straight-up blood-soaked (well, without any actual blood) dungeon crawl, which surprised me.  I thought here would be more puzzles and story and stuff.  It feels very much like a video game ported to a boardgame format; complete with a finite number of "extra lives" before you lose the game.

It also really difficult, unless I'm playing the combat rules wrong.

While the designers do a good job of varying the 11 scenarios included with the game; every new room (with a handful of exceptions) is a new battle, so each "Chapter is a succession of 6 or 7 battles against combinations of the same 5 or 6 enemy types, plus 4 bosses.

Currently finished Chapter 3 and it's already feeling kind of samey.

UPDATE: Having finished the base game I can say that this one was perfect to play with my kids, and is the Dungeons & Dragons game I wished I had had when I was in elementary school.  

I can't see this holding the interest of a group of adults, however, without house rules to either eliminate lots of combat or vary it significantly.

RATING: 8
The theme is great.  The first few times I played it, we always seemed to have new players and only ever played Chapter 1 (i.e. the intro scenario). Then a few of us decided to start a campaign and that meant playing the other chapters (in fact, we skipped Chapter 1 because we'd all played it so much). The rules aren't always clear--the rulebook prioritizes theme over clarity--but the designer has made official rulings on most of the ambiguities. And you're probably fine with whatever ruling you decide on your own if you don't want to track down the FAQs. The campaign rules do a pretty good job of providing a way to grow your characters without unbalancing it too much for the person who just wants to play the chapters in isolation.

RATING: N/A
Played a few times with a playtest version.

It's rather different than both Summoner Wars and Dungeon Run, as well as most other "dungeon crawls" on the market.

It's a fun game to play with family and friends.  Bistro's writing, John Ariosa's art, and Jerry Hawthorne's design and setting mixed with simple mechanics really works if this is the kind of game you're looking for.  If you're no stranger to dice, want your game to tell a story and want a co-op, I recommend it.

If you want a tactical masterpiece or to see your foes driven before you, or want to play most efficiently all the time... you might not be reading this anywyay.

P.S.  Forgot Chad's minis.  Excellent.  Paint the centipedes and leave them in your wife's jewelry drawer.

RATING: 5
2013-02-01

Initial Rating: 6.5 (January 2013)

I was pleasantly surprised by the game, this is a familiar looking, dungeon crawler game. I would have never played it due to its theme, it just doesn’t call to me. After I played it I found it to be a little boring. However, it is a good game to play with some close friends. 

The components are great, the minis are very well done and they look gorgeous when painted (I will upload pictures of this). The rules are, relatively, simple so it is ideal to introduce new players or family to the hobby. The theme works well and the story is engaging. I would like to play all the scenarios with the same game group BUT I have other campaign games I want to play over this one (Descent, Gears of War, Earth Reborn, Risk Legacy) so perhaps this won’t see much play. 

I have played only the first scenario and it was fun but extremely easy, I really hope the game racks up the difficulty in later scenarios. 

It appears the game has a lot of luck, but as it is a light game I can live with that. I also like how each turn you have to shuffle the initiative track but that adds to the randomness.  

Bottom line, I prefer to play heavier games than this but it is a good light game to play with friends and family.

Current Rating: 6.5
[hr]
2014-05-19

As I´m currently reviewing my ratings, I can’t in good conscience give Mice & Mystics a rating higher than 5.0. The game is great looking, but the theme is in disagreement with my tastes AND it is way too simple for me.

I would consider it for my children if I had any. Desire to play M&M is very low.

The game play is arguably even a little too simplistic; it's not going to replace any of the great tactical minis games you might love. But if you play with younger folk, or anyone who is a fan of young adult fantasy (or Redwall or Watership Down), this might just be a good fit.

7/12/2015 - I'm dropping my rating because I honestly just don't have a lot of desire to play this, especially when stacked up against other coop dungeon crawlers like Gears of War or Galaxy Defenders.

2018-01-15 - And, I'm upping my rating back up from a 6 to a 7. This game has found new life for me as a good way to get to know my little, and his enthusiasm for the game and story have helped me appreciate it more.

RATING: 8.5

They are perfect for beer and pretzels, this game is perfect for sitting with great people and playing through a story. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Mice and Mystics is a simple - almost too simple - adventure game with an incredibly appealing theme. If I was a deep fan of dungeon crawlers, I don't think the theme would be enough to compensate for the lack of interesting mechanics and rules. That said, my wife - who is not an experienced adventurer - likes the theme a lot and has little other experience to compare it to, so we've been moving through the campaign two-player and we are enjoying it. I had scored this an "8", but I think it more objectively deserves a 7. Not only are the rules a bit too simple, but they are not clearly laid out in the rule book, either.

Another reason I'm dropping this a point is because - although the story line is pretty good - the scenario intros and in-adventure text can include characters that are not in play for that adventure. This could have been avoided (and I believe they did fix this in Downwood Tales). It is distracting when the story uses characters that clearly are not present in the room when being read.

UPDATE: After completing 7 scenarios, my wife admitted that the mechanics aren't interesting and the story is not keeping her hooked. Dropped this another point and will sell. mechanically, the game really is a 5, I've decided, and there isn't enough variety. Gets a "6" though for the unique and appealing theme.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Wow I honestly can't believe the hype surrounding this game because it just fell so flat with my group. I was really excited to play it; so excited in fact that I preordered it. Boy was I disappointed! I played it about 3 times and each time it actually got worse! 

Here's the main problem I have with this game. The ending of each play through is dictated completely randomly by the rolls of the enemies. Basically if they roll a cheese than it adds one cheese to the cheese wheel. Dying also causes the cheese wheel to fill up. If the wheel fills up a certain amount of times game over. I absolutely despise this mechanic. It makes the ending so arbitrary. We could all be doing so well and then all of a sudden just lose out of nowhere. 2 hours wasted because of randomness. Why couldn't they just make the round end after a certain amount of deaths. It just really ruins it for us. Sure we could just pretend it didn't happen but cheating on a coop game just feels lame and it should just work well out of the box.

Just to add on to the problems, there are very few different enemies and abilities so combat gets old quick. I really really really wanted to like it. I love the theme and think that Plaid Hat did a really good job with the production but the flaws really make this game a boring drag. Please try before you buy!

RATING: 10
This game is an incredible system highly reminiscent of heroquest style games with lots of dice rolling, and battling minis.  I simply love the artwork on the tiles, and appreciate the effort that went into making the movement spaces organically integrated into the art of the tile, rather than just doing lazy squares for grid combat.  The story and some of the battle mechanics are great...love that they came up with achievements that give you special bonuses.  I can't wait until my daughter is old enough to play this as I am sure she will have a blast.  I played this with my friends (late 20's) and brother (16) and we all had a good time, despite my reservations that the kid friendly theme might make the game seem dull (it didn't at all)

RATING: 10
Fall 2012...Just got it, looking forward to playing...

Late May 2014...After a year and a half, where other things and games kept getting in the way, I finally got started on M&M... I played a solo game, something I otherwise never do, to get a feel for the rules before playing with my game group... I flipped through the rules a lot, but got the hang of it, and though I made a couple of small mistakes here and there, it wasn't anything really unbalancing the game... I played the first chapter, did the Miz Maggie side plot, and managed to haul a group of wounded mice to the hole in the tree, just two cheeses away from a game ending surge... GREAT GAME!

Early June 2014... Just bought the two lost chapters from PHG, and the promo cards from the BGG store... Looking very much forward to Downwood Tales...

September 2015... I have Heart of Glorm and Downwood Tales as well. Have given up on ever playing this with my Thursday gaming group, as campaign style games are not really suitable for that... But plan to start playing with my daughter this weekend...

And so we did! Well worth the three year wait! Playing with Emma, at age six was a blast! Two characters each, and we played through the entire first chapter in one go, and she can't wait to play again... 
First weekend we played Capters one and two, and are halfway through Chapter three...

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
CRITIQUE OF MICE & MYSTICS
I have a brief review of Mice & Mystics [thread=958027]here[/thread].

Given my long history with roleplaying games (going back to 1979), I had high hopes for Mice & Mystics. The components looked great, the story-based play seemed immersive, and it was from the same publisher that produced Summoner Wars! Unfortunately, the game did not live up to my high expectations.

Gameplay in M&M is frustrating and tedious. It's frustrating because the rulebook is poorly written, with no examples of play, and this interferes with the players' immersion in the story. Read the flavor text to start an adventure, equip your mice, and start playing, then... "Wait! How does that rule for switching weapons work again? Oh, the rulebook is ambiguous? Better take a break while checking BGG forums for the answer." In the meantime, any sense of immersion is lost.

It's also frustrating because there is no way to mitigate the luck that dominates the game. Admittedly, the custom dice are very well done, but everything in the game is decided by rolling them. The gameplay in M&M works like this: roll dice to move, roll dice to attack, roll dice for defense, roll more dice to move, roll more dice to attack, roll more dice to defend, etc. Oh, and occasionally you get to roll dice to search... if you have time. You get the idea. It quickly become a tedious exercise in passing the dice tray back and forth between us.

For a game that we all wanted to love, it is incredibly disappointing that we all find ourselves relieved when we complete a chapter. We aren't satisfyingly relieved that we completed the mission, we are just glad that the game is over, because the game is just one tedious combat after another. And the game forces you to kill every enemy on a tile before you can move on! Often, combat will cause a surge to happen and even more enemies appear. We didn't hate surges because they made the chapter more difficult; we hated them because they led to more tedious combat. By the game's end we have all had it. Two hours of this is more than enough.

There's no doubt that M&M can be challenging, but like an old-school RPG it's challenging because of what you roll rather than how you play. Roll too much cheese for the wheel and more enemies appear. Roll well on your enemies' defense and they become harder to kill. Roll poorly on your movement and you can't get to them quickly enough. But none of these are actually choices you make. The game makes these decisions for you. There are precious few decisions to be made, because the stories are linear and there is really only one thing each mouse can do.

The rulebook is inadequate in some crucial places, and you have to find answers to very basic questions either on BGG or by watching video walkthroughs. But the thing that finally sunk the game for me was the fact that the game's designer frequently responded to questions about the rules using the words, "technically yes, but..." In other words, even the game's designer isn't sure how the game is supposed to be played. This should just never happen with a board game.

The one place this game shines is in its theme, but even this is flawed. The enemies are too few, and their scale makes no sense. Why is a cockroach nearly as tough as a rat? How can the mice fight Brody the cat at all? For a game that prides itself on a well-integrated theme the way that theme is applied seems sloppy. And of course it's difficult to stay connected with the story when every action you take feels exactly the same.

I have no idea why this game made it into the top 100 here, because for us it was a major disappointment.

RATING: 6.5
I am only 2 chapters in. I am a big fan of the artwork and components. I enjoy the story book vibe of it as well as the little narrative breaks in between gameplay. Each character feels unique in their available abilities as well, which for any RPG is a must for me. Even with all these pluses there is just something about the game that just hasn't completely hooked me yet. 

I think it is the fact that there is no DM. On paper I thought this was a huge plus. This means that you can play it solo and no one is stuck DMing if they don't want to. But to me, in practice, it makes the game feel a little less tight and overall less fun. For starters it means that enemy behavior is completely predictable. The only variability is going to be their dice rolls. I mean, the system they have set up with the initiative track, custom dice and system for enemy behavior certainly works. It just all seems a little bit "meh" to me.

RATING: 7
This game is a solid dungeon crawler with an imaginative theme and a great story. Any fan of DnD and Redwall/Mouseguard will instantly love this. I am currently through the first three chapters of the game and I am surprised of how difficult this game can be even with its cute furry theme. The game is challenging, engaging, and exciting. Everything that I look for in a dungeon crawler. Component quality is good. Miniatures look great. Cards and bits are on par. The custom dice are great. Tiles feel heavy and showcase great attention to detail art. One of my biggest gripes with this game is that it caps at 4, and could have easily been scaled for more. Quests can take a little longer than what it feels like, but overall there is much more to like here than dislike. One that I will be playing for a while.

RATING: 7
Mice and Mystics is a cooperative adventure game in which the players work together to save an imperiled kingdom. They will face countless adversaries such as rats, cockroaches, and spiders, and of course the greatest of all horrors: the castle's housecat, Brodie. Mice and Mystics is a boldly innovative game that thrusts players into an ever-changing, interactive environment, and features a rich storyline that the players help create as they play the game. The Cheese System allows players to hoard the crumbs of precious cheese they find on their journey, and use it to bolster their mice with grandiose new abilities and overcome seemingly insurmountable odds.

================================================

Enjoyable and light dungeon crawl but with mice and a lighter story line.  (Think Redwall!)  There are some rule questions that frequently came up but have largely been resolved.  Each mouse has different abilities and starting armor/weapons so each character does play differently.  The timing mechanism can be aggravating if one rolls lots of cheese on the monster attack/defense rolls.  Plays fairly quickly once you get the hang of your choices.  Game play does start being repetitive fairly quickly though...

Do yourself a favor and read this well crafted and sentimental review: http://fortressat.com/articles-boardgame-reviews/4032-mice-and-mystics-review

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
First of all, this game is certainly not for everyone. If you are not into the rich story or the unique theme, this game is a fairly run of the mill dungeon crawl (or at least of the co-op variety). However, for those who do like reading the flavor text this game's story arc immerses you deeply into the theme (although the great artwork and the scenarios having a bit more variety than say Castle Ravenloft doesn't hurt either). Furthermore, there are very few good anthropomorphic animal games out there, especially ones without silly artwork.

I really like how they did leveling up with this game. It allows you to have the feeling that your character is growing without making playing in a non-campaign mode too much of a disadvantage. Also, death (captured) is a good balance of making you feel like you are losing your character (since you lose equipped items) without making you twiddle your thumbs for the rest of the game (your mouse can respawn after the current fight is over).

While most adventures require you to play 4 mice, I have not had too much trouble playing this as a 2 player or solo experience besides lapsing on minor scenario-specific rules.

The basic rules I feel are simple enough for a child or nongamer to learn but you definitely need someone who knows what they're doing for the more specific stuff.

I wish the strategy level of this game was a bit higher. The main optimizations seem to involve positioning of your mice (healing has a pretty short range in this game, but you can also kite enemies if you spread out more) and cheese management depending on your team, besides a few more minor things. However, I feel like a lot of time strategy is overridden by luck. This especially seems the case if you get a lot of cheese added to the cheese wheel early, as not only do you have to deal with surges, but the minions you will face will be more difficult due to the increased chapter number, creating a snow ball effect.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
A dungeon, adventure game where the characters are mice and there is a story built around the game.  It is a very well written story and you fight rats, cockroaches, spiders and other "boss" monsters like the cat.  

However the game is really complex for kids.  At least one adult has to be a gamer as the game rules can be fiddly with a number of exceptions.  There scenarios are really hard, which can be very disappointing for young children.  Another issue is that combat becomes repetitive.  This game is a good example of the Dice Tower over-hyping a game.  

Having said all this, it is a solid game and if you insulate your kids from the complexity, you will have a good time.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
It is a game wrapped around a story.  The gameplay itself is rather shallow, simplistic, and very luck driven.  There is a minimal sense of progression, and some of the limited number of character skills are not particularly exciting.  The game also tends to last too long for its lack of depth and player choice.

The components are incredible, the story is cute, and it all works thematically.  You will get your money's worth out of it playing with kids who do not mind heavy repetition of gameplay and of encounters.  Losing a chapter after an hour+ of gameplay to just have to trudge through that chapter again - which will play out rather similarly - is not fun for most adults.

We played as much as we did only so we could make our way through some of the storyline, and, ultimately, we just couldn't take it anymore.  The gameplay could not sustain our interest.  There are better co-operative games with more tension and more teamwork, and there are better dungeon crawlers of both co-operative and versus varieties.  Frankly, there are better story-driven games and games which create or embrace a personal or group narrative.  Ultimately, really, the story and cuteness which holds up the game is out-matched by a single Redwall novel or Mouse Guard comic, and they take a heck of a lot less time to enjoy.

RATING: 9
052.16. 10.may.13 - CSI: 49,99-0,89+21,64
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Before buying this game, you will have to decide, if you want to play it with your adult friends or with your kids.

If you want to play this with your friends, just don't:
this is by far the dullest coop dungeon crawler I have played thus far, and I have played quite a few.

EVERYTHING you do is decided by dice rolling or other forms of randomness. you want to move? roll a die to determine your speed. you want to search? roll a die to see if you find something. oh, you found something? draw a card to see if it is good or bad. you want to get out of the water? roll a die to see if you succeed. you want to fight? roll the dice (ok, this one is in every dungeon crawler.) you rolled a cheese symbol on an enemies attack? put a cheese token on the wheel (cheese tokens on the wheel may end your game quite soon, so whether you win or loose can also be decided by randomness!!! what?! YES!!!)

the AI is dull, like in every other coop dungeon crawler, but this one manages to make it even duller. you are actually forced to kill every monster in a room before you are allowed to advance into the next one. meaning, all you do in a room is roll dice for combat. you don't even have to move actually, because the monster will move towards you anyway and positioning is completely irrelevant, too, so why bother moving?!?! oh, and if you are looking for monster variation, you will not find it here, because there are maybe 4 or 5 different types, which makes everything even more boring.

hands down, if you have ever played and loved descent or even simpler games like dungeons and dragons: castle ravenloft (and those others), then you should run away from this one, because it is DULL. did I say that already? Well, it is.

if you want to play this with your kids:
the above criticized simplicity is obviously not a big deal, since it must be simple enough for kids to understand and play. 

also, the theme and the story are a plus-point for kids. 

however, even for kids the cheese-wheel is a deal breaker in my eyes. why they implemented this mechanic is beyond me. as soon as you have rolled too many cheese symbols, you loose the game. so even, if your heroes are all still well and healthy the game is over. I find this very annoying.

another thing is that heroes can be captured by the enemies (also randomly). this means, you have to wait and skip your turn for as long as you are rescued again or the game is over. this certainly is not fun for kids.

overall, I cannot recommend this game to anyone.

RATING: 7
The trouble with Mice and Mystics is all that it [i]could have[/i] been.  The interactivity of the story book had me wanting a choose your own adventure style campaign but instead left us just playing the same chapters again until we got to the next page the way the game wanted us to.  The storybook theme, which drips wonderfully from the game, pushed me to want the gameplay to be less fiddly and have the smoothness, almost sing-songy cadence of a children’s book.  Even the story itself was a bit lackluster compared to similar attempts in other media to capture the melancholy potential of the bed time story.  Were it not for all the “[i]could haves[/i]”, the game could have been something very special instead of just polite.  Here is hoping the expansions seize the greater potential in the format.

RATING: 8
What a fun little game! Story based fairy tale with simple mechanics, but enough interesting choices.  It's wonderfully evocative artwork and adorable mice minis immerse you in the theme.

For me the story elevates Mice and Mystics above Castle Ravenloft (which I traded many moons ago).  Both are fairly predictable dungeon crawls, but when you play Mice and Mystics you feel like you're on a grand adventure.  The artwork is wonderfully evocative and the minis are adorable. There's no other game quite like it so I think it definitely earns a spot in any gamer's collection.  At least it does in mine.

RATING: 7
I was very excited to play this as a family game with my wife, 6 year old son, and 9 year old daughter.  It is definitely being enjoyed by the kids and the story aspect is awesome.  I love the art and the overall component quality, but the gameplay itself really hasn't grabbed me and my wife just barely tolerates it.  It has pretty standard, simple miniatures mechanisms to move and attack, so there's really nothing new there.  The special ability cards generally don't seem to add much to the game other than slightly modifying your odds, so the variety in actions is fairly low.  We've only played through a few chapters so far but we've had to divide each one into multiple play sessions, so the overall progress feels a bit slow.  On the whole I think the story element and theme are what really make this game work.  Based purely on gameplay I don't think there's anything new or exciting here and, as such, this is not something I would offer to bring out with a group of 'gamers'.

RATING: 8
I don't like the current trend of games costing more than the average price. 

This said MnM is well worth it:

While you don't get a lot of models they are very well done (Centipede is particularly excellent) with unique models for each mouse a major bonus. Unique art on most cards and heavy duty tiles and chits also adds to this deserved price tag. Just a stunning production. Children and easily excitable gamers will wet themselves.

Possibly not the most elegant game design ever but thematically a masterpiece. Wonderful story and magical items that'll warm those initially cold to the setting. 

Gameplay wise it's a dungeon crawler with all the usual limitations that this brings. If you want the tactically deepest dungeon crawler then its probably descent, the most elegant and best bang for your buck Claustrophobia but if you want a solid dungeon crawler that's readily accessible, with very strong theme, campaign elements, very high production values and like the idea of mice or a setting that's not the same old fantasy- this is it.

RATING: 7
5 years of extensive DnD sessions, may have "burned" most Dungeon Crawler games, but from time to time, some of them can give something new and different. Mice and Mystics, is not about deep strategies and a bag full of monster miniatures. It is a great theme-based, storytelling, co-op game with light rules, that let you enjoy the heart of the game, which is its great story. Could play anytime, with the right group, that likes to play the games in-character. Also I can imagine this one as a great game for children, as one that can keep them hanging on for the rest of the story after each mission of its fantastic Campaign.

RATING: 6
Better than I expected it to be. The rules are a little convoluted...not to mention nebulous here and there...and the game does suffer from low variation beyond playing the scenarios, but the game is actually pretty fun. The characters feel different, there's nice variety with items and skills, and there are enough enemies to not feel like they're too repetitive. I don't think it's one I would ever go out and buy, but I can see how it works well as a family game. My only major complaint is that you can be playing an hour-long scenario and lose completely out of the blue. This is a bit anti-climactic, but at least the game isn't a cake walk, I suppose. Pretty fun, but nothing amazing.

RATING: 9.5
Really neat RPG-type campaign game.  There are just a couple minor issues: 1) We are finding we need to buy additional pieces to keep the game on track.  For example, the "search" action is only valid for one successful search per mouse per room.  In order to keep track of who has successfully searched a room (2 players playing with 2 mice each), we had to add buttons to the game container.  We have noticed the same issue with the cheese - if someone becomes the Cheesemaster, it burns through a lot of cheese really quickly; 2) rules are laid out in a way that are a little difficult to follow. Would benefit from crib sheets.
Hoping that there will be an expansion that adds a fifth player option soon.

RATING: 8
After one play today with my wife and daughter I can say the game play is a little on the fiddly side, but it is the first time I have ever played a dungeon crawl type game so that may be par for the course. After a while though we go a hold of it and got on a roll. It does seem close to impossible to complete the side quest though, but I think I may have been playing a rule wrong when I was doing the movement between the tiles.

Art work is gorgeous, story is engaging, my daughter who is only 5 cared so much about her little mouse figure and that was great to see. My wife, who is not a gamer, even got into the spirit of the game to a certain extent which was great to see. She may have just been humouring me though as I know it is definitely not her thing.

Any way. I like it. Possibly love it enough to overlook its occasional clunkiness. I am not sure how to streamline the clunk out of it though so I think it is as good as it could be.

8.5 after the first play through, will see how they go from there.

RATING: 7
In this cooperative dungeon crawl game, players are mice, attempting to defeat monsters while trying to achieve the victory conditions for a particular scenario.

What makes this game unique are the humorous items in the game, such as getting cheese, meeting rats and the various items the mice can search for and pick up. 

This game is enjoyble for a light hearted game, and you could play with kids. It's one of those games where you read the scenario word for word to enjoy the theme of being turned into a mouse. There is luck with the dice rolling, and appears to be more so than other dungeon crawl games. If you want a little deeper game, consider Legends of Andor.

RATING: 6
There's a lot to like about this game, from the art, to the theme to the story. Overall it's a great game. But, for me it suffers in a few areas that just brings the rating down:

1. The base game doesn't offer a lot of variety in enemies.
2. The dice rolling can be frustrating. I have a tendency to lose all my mice very easily and lose the chapter mission.
3. The rules is clunky or confusing in places requiring regular rulebook checks or looking things up on BGG (especially since each chapter may have new rules to follow). This is made especially difficult by the absence of any quick reference sheets.

Overall the rules are much too obtuse for the type of game it is. This is a problem with games that want to be really thematic. They require so many rules and side cases, that nothing is intuitive.

RATING: 5
----- Preliminary thoughts -----
It's very similar to the D&D boardgames (Castle Ravenloft, etc.), simpler but with a better story (special for kids!), even better art, less monsters, custom dice and a couple of different mechanics.

There are a couple of great things about this game:
-> Components are amazing, moderls are great and art is fantastic. Even the manual is beautiful. 
-> The whole game revolves about the story: there is a story book with the chapters; onve they are over, the game doesn't seem to have great replayability.
-> The mechanic for rolling cheese is very attractive, but I guess you will get tired of it quite soon.

It seems there are not enough reasons to buy the game (considering I already have the 3 D&D games). I'm specially concerned about the replayability.

RATING: 5
This is a tough one to rate. I really wanna like it more, because it is just beautifully made, there is so much love for details and I appreciate the story of it a lot, but the overall gameplay is just not really that appealing for me.  
It's too much rolling of the same dice overall, which becomes a little too repetitive for me to enjoy it for how long the game plays. This is even more of a problem as you can not play with less characters when you have less players, so you actually have to roll for all of them and compared to similar games this also does not really let you "connect" so well to "your" character as you just play several of them.

I still think there is a lot of heart in this and whenever I have kids I guess it's great to introduce them into a light coop game with a really great story and if not it still is a keeper for me just to have as an artpiece and maybe I'll even get it out for the sake of the story.

RATING: 8
Je m'étais procuré Mice & Mystics dans l'optique de me replonger dans l'univers d'Hero Quest qui avait bercé mon enfance. Effectivement je ne fus pas déçu :-). Même mieux finalement puisqu'il est possible de jouer seul vu qu'il n'y a pas de maitre de jeu. La partie solo est bien, cela permet d'expérimenter un chapitre avant de le faire découvrir à d'autres joueurs : ça peut être bien pour éviter de perdre du temps à se replonger systématiquement dans les règles car il y en a un sacré paquet dans ce jeu! Mice & Mystics arrive à rallier richesse et simplicité de jeu. J'ai beau enchainer les parties, aucune ne ressemble : c'est vraiment très plaisant. Avec ses 11 chapitres il y a de quoi faire avant de se jeter sur les extensions pour prolonger l'histoire. D'ailleurs un des points forts du jeu est bien son histoire : contée telle un conte de fées, l'immersion et l'aventure sont au rendez vous. A ne manquer donc sous aucun prétexte ;-)
