RATING: 7.95
A very different gaming experience! I really enjoy playing the mice as they travel from story to story. The game is completely scripted (as is Legends of Andor). I don't mind this type of game, but my wife really isn't a great fan of the style because it really effects replay ability. But we both agree that if you haven't played this game in say 6 months, I think you could replay all the stories again and have a good time. And if you were in a strong mood to play several of the stories back to back...I think you would be well satisfied that you got a lot of fun for your money.

The rulebook is heavy with rules...constantly going back to be sure you are following the correct way to play. It can be frustrating at how many times you will need to refer back. The information is there, concisely written and easy to understand. As you play more of the stories, you begin to get the rules down and things move along. 

A nice game for families especially. A sort of fairy tale type adventure that is very appropriate for kids. But be advised parents, you will be reading a lot of rules and guiding your kids through several stories before they might be able to continue on their own.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I applaud the attempt to provide a different theme, being more family friendly I guess. And it was fresh for a first-time play as a result. I'm just not sure I want to play a campaign of adventures where I'm being mice beating up rats and roaches before I get to go where I need to go - and doing this same thing in every single room. Otherwise it has all the same features as your typical dungeon crawl adventure game - equip your character, move and battle (or battle and move), roll dice for combat, take wounds and so on. I liked the cheese wheel - if a baddie rolls a cheese instead of sword or shield, it adds a cheese to the cheese wheel and when that is filled the game is progressed plus more baddies come out. If they roll well in battle therefore, less baddies comes out; if they roll poorly in battle, more baddies come out. Nice. The co-op decisions are who's going to battle who (which is usually pretty straight forward) and if you're going to search for more equipment (each player has a 50% chance of finding something, via a die roll, in each room) before you collectively consider the room finished and you all move simultaneously to the next room to start anew. So the emphasis is on sharing the journey, not so much the quality of the decision making. To that end, the scenarios are full of thematic fluff to read out and live. It's designed to play as a campaign with the same players - stuff you pick up in the first scenario can be used in the next. I'd happily play if others wanted because it's pleasantly easy, but I'd hope that future scenarios provide more room to room variety than the first scenario did.

RATING: 4
A little too light for what it is. Not many interesting decisions. Don't really see any re-play value to this game due to the simplistic mechanics and lack of meatiness to the game play. There is a serious lack of luck mitigation and probability management. 

The game feels about on par with the Dungeons and Dragons co-op board games. Though slightly better due to the theme and good story interlaced through the missions. Slightly more variability and narrative in what you experience during the game. Not as mechanical and dry. 

I do wish the game had a little more depth to it. It doesn't have to be Descent, but something more than roll dice and hope you succeed would have been preferable. I believe the target audience for this game is: Dad's who want a game to play with their 6-9 year olds that isn't Candyland or Sorry. In that regard it's an excellent game.

However we will definitely play the entire campaign due to the good story attached, but then it is getting sold off. The game looks like it will take about 20hrs of game time.

Game components look great, but are of a poor manufacturing quality. Cards are getting scuffed with almost no use to them yet. Tiles are mashing at the corners and we only just started playing! 

I've been babying this thing since opening it. I can only imagine the horrors of what will happen when kids get their hands on the game. Adult supervision only.

Game feels a little expensive for what you get in the box comparatively to other similarly equipped games.

edit: Bah! Want to like this game but the game play is starting to grate. Don't have it in me to finish the campaign due to the game play  getting so dull after awhile. This is getting sold off.

RATING: 9
The game art on this game is awesome. The theme is great. Very enjoyable.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
A great pure co-op dungeon crawler with a cute story attached. I've so far really enjoyed going through the story chapters with my five-year-old daughter. 

I really like the innovative initiative track encounter design, it's one of the best additions to the genre I've ever seen and I'm surprised this hasn't been used before. It really shakes up the standard set rotation of turns, adds excitement to the start of every new encounter (especially since some mice get advantages depending on their position on the track). Combat is simple and fun, I like that the dice are the same for everything, and the success ratio feels pretty good for each action. Sure, there's luck (it's dice) but we really haven't felt a whole lot of bad luck whammies. And mostly, when Nez is rolling all five dice on a Battle Squeak attack, he's going to kill or seriously wound whatever is on the receiving end of his hammer. 

Okay, complaints... It can't all be good, right? Well, it mostly is. Really the only complaint I have is the price to packaging discrepancy. I'm happy with the game, I think that the contents are worth the MSRP (I was initially a little underwhelmed by the low number of miniatures for such a costly game, but the gorgeous full color rulebook and especially the 50+ page storybook make up for that). But I do feel, that if you're going to create a game with fantastic artwork on really big cardboard tiles, well, you probably don't want to let those tiles just slide around loose in the box. My copy came with one damaged tile and some others that had wear and tear on the sides right out of the box. A simple shrink wrap job would have prevented this. Live and learn, I suppose. And for the record, when I contacted Plaid Hat about sending a replacement I received a response in less than a minute. As long as the replacement arrives in a timely fashion then my only real complaint about this thing will be just a minor annoyance in the rear view mirror.

RATING: 7
Positive: very, very beautiful artwork! Also a very good tutorial video on the website of Plaid Had Games. If you lose your lifepoints, you're captured and not death. You can still re-enter the game if your companions can clear the room.

Negative: quality of the components: cards are clearly China print and get wear by just lookig at them. So if you already have some co-operative games and are looking for a game that will offers you something really new, I'm afraid this game won't do it for you.

RATING: 7
 A well-written fantasy adventure campaign game with cute little mouse minis. The battle system is nothing unusual, but it does have a nice 'common-sense' mentality of which spaces are adjacent and it plays very simply compared to some other games in the genre.

The rulebook leaves a little to be desired in terms of clarity. It should be mentioned that no matter how many players you have, you always use four hero figures on the board, which we were not aware of in our first play. As we were playing just the first level we encountered a number of questions that weren't clear from what was written in the rulebook.

Overall, this is a fun, easy, dice-roll-y team adventure game with no overlord, which is refreshing.

:star: Art and components
:nostar: Innovative mechanics
:nostar: Handles 5 or more players
:star: Good with min or max players
:star: Low time between turns
:star: Comfortable complexity
:star: Re-playability
:star::star::nostar: Enjoyment

RATING: 9.5
Probably the best dungeon crawler out there. There's a lot of heart and thought put into this box. The story is phenomenal and it's one of those rare games, where the story is first class citizen - you play for the story, you anxiously await what will happen next. The story allows for a development of a connection with characters. Yes, the story is about mice, about love, courage, treachery and evil. It looks like a fairy tale, but adults should be able to appreciate the story too. It doesn't try to be pretentious or infantile like most of "generic fantasy" games do (looking at you, Descent). 

Also, it's a dungeon crawler where you cooperate, instead "evil guy vs the rest" approach. While it still has all the problems of cooperation games (alpha gamer, etc.), it's refeshing approach to feel that for once, "we're all in this together now". There are very cool and neatly tied mechanics here - initiative order, special abilities, flipping tiles to provide "3d" feeling, oh my. Do you know any other game, where you can lay down a fork, place a grape on it, and then catapult it towards your enemies, tacking the grape tile into your hand and flipping it like a coin? If it lands on a splat side, you've guessed it - it landed well :)

Miniatures are superbly done. 

I like this game very very much. I thought that the constant dice rolling will be a problem for me, but it isn't. I understand the thought behind this game - there should be luck, there should be misfortune, that's how it is and your job is to try to mitigate this as good as you can. It's not a game of "grind mobs and quickly level up, build a massive combo and then steamroll over your opponents". There is no feeling of "winning more". You're allowed to tweak your equipment a bit, but you're always in danger. It's the skill in positioning, using cheese for your abilities in the right time and exchanging equipement/cheese, that matters. 

I feel that there is enough space for meaningful decisions there and it's a challenge older players will gladly pick up (how to maximize our time, our abilities and push our luck). 

What I would prefer in future expansions, to introduce a bit more color to this. The game's palette is quite gloomy, mostly black/red/brown. It maintains a consistent theme, but I wouldn't mind to stray away from this for a while in future campaign and get some bright colours and light.

-0.5 points, because I feel it's not perfect and some more mechanics other than battle/search would be interesting. Also, while I don't mind the manual (it's actually quite well written, contrary to what you might have heard), I guess that there are many rare situations you might bump into, and the official FAQ doesn't cover them well. I believe it should be expanded.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This game has a lot in common with other dungeon crawler games. Essentially a race against the clock and bad guys pour out of every crevice. The search deck is filled with lots of interesting goodies and the variety in abilities each mice can learn increases the replay value quite a bit. The story is a bit sophomoric but it doesn't stop each mission from being highly entertaining. The unique setting/environments go a long way.

Almost everything functions with the roll of the dice. This is both Mice & Mystics greatest strength and weakness. A lot is gained from the simplicity, but sometimes a few bad roles will end your mission prematurely. It's rare the mice have enough time to fully explore all the options available to them.

Overall: A very impressive game built on fairly simple mechanics. Lighter than most similar games, yet provides plenty of challenge to keep things interesting. Looking forward to many more quests!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Really love the artwork and components for this game - it is very visually appealing.  Combat is simple but I think that is for the best - it keeps things moving along!  The how to play movie on Plaid Hat Games was well done and very much appreciated - it makes teaching the game basics quite easy.  There are a few things not mentioned in the video, but not many.

My only complaint?  Certain scenarios can limit the number of players.  Our group of four had a lot of fun, but chapter 2 wasn't as much fun because one person had very little to do due to story constraints. 

Still, I highly recommend this one.  Everyone in our group was impressed and asking where to get a copy for their families.

RATING: 8.3
This has the potential to be a very engaging and intriguing story, dungeon crawl type game.  Thick with story and that was enjoyable.  Unfortunately, i played my first game incorrectly which made it much harder on me than it should had been which was frustrating.  Lots of small little rules that can be overlooked and I wish they had a player aid in the box. 

However, with my second play this is just a great adventure that isn't too fiddly  and just immerses you in the theme.  there is some vagueness with the rules and cards but this is the type of game that is a story and experience not a competitive game.  Frankly, it just a fun ride that so far is really close between success and defeat.  

After the third game, i find this game actually difficult to manage all the character and rules as solo game so I screw up the rules a bit but i think I would have still had success. No matter really as I think the purpose of the game is entertainment and adventure rather than deep strategic though and strict rules.

RATING: 5
Heroquest with mice. Your mileage on this will depend a lot on how cute you find furry little rodents with swords, spells, and bows. If you enjoyed the Redwall books you'll probably love it. If the theme doesn't really grab you then the game play is not really on a par with a lot of other dungeon questing type games (and in the co-operative vein particularly the D&D Ravenloft and Ashcalon - can't remember how to spell that one). 
The mechanics are pretty straight forward and what you would expect, move, roll dice to attack, roll dice to defend, use special abilities. Monsters spawn in various places, kill them, search for stuff, reach an objective.
Its not a bad game but the theme didn't grab me (well except one quite fun moment with the mouse fork catapult - but there weren't enough of those moments).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
The biggest gaming disappointment of 2012 for me. What promised to be a unique co-operative adventure experience (bear in mind that I don't normally enjoy co-operative games, but I had heard so many good things about this one that I decided I wanted it anyway) turns out to be, when shorn of the hype, a totally generic roll-dice-and-fight-monsters game. The much-heralded "cheese system" is nothing original, just a very basic (and randomly determined) resource system for upgrading your characters. The rulebook is another big disappointment - it is long and lavishly produced, but leaves many things ambiguous and even leaves out at least one important rule (that you can't move against the current in water).

About the only reason this game didn't go on our list of games to trade is that, while it didn't work with my gaming group, the story-based campaign is kind of nice and it might be appealing to our son (currently 2) when he is a bit older. It's OK, but aside from the story - which isn't even all that original - this game really has no reason for existing.
Having got all that off my chest, this isn't actually a bad game - and the theme is the one truly unique selling point, it's both original and quite endearing, particularly if you have a group that likes following a story over several game nights (my groups don't). But the game itself - while perfectly playable and even enjoyable - doesn't really do anything new or interesting enough to justify the game's cost or its high rating.

RATING: 8.8
It´s a great adventure boardgame with an outstanding production design, a very nice artwork, and with an accomplished atmosphere. It´s a truly delight to play it! It´s considered a great (dice) game for introducing neophytes in boardgames like role-fantasy-adventure ones, but I think that maybe sometimes the game could be a little bit difficult because some rules are not clear enough, and some chapters (like Chapter 9) are very, VERY difficult to achive a victory. Also, its mechanic can be a little bit repetitive, so I recomend give some time between chapter and chapter. It´s one of the most beautiful boardgames I have in my collection, and I highly recommended it.

RATING: 4
I was pretty disappointed - after all the hype, I was really hoping for an engrossing story-based game that my kids would enjoy, but it kind of flopped.  After I read the prologue and scenario and went through the first turn, my daughter was like "We need to get this game!" but after many more turns, my son had already left the table and my daughter said "Yeah, I guess we already have a lot better game than this."  It might partly be because I was learning the rules and had to keep checking things, but the story aspect just doesn't come through in the game play.  The game boils down to "read a paragraph about the new tile, roll a lot of dice fighting minions, repeat." You might occasionally get a new item or very rarely get a new skill, but it's also very likely that you will die ("captured") and restart without your items or cheese stockpile needed to use your skills (Maginos was our only character that never died, thanks to invisibility).  It's quite fiddly rules-wise (similar to many theme-heavy games), and could definitely benefit from some general and chapter-specific player aids.  And being a coop, it can lead to some players being led along and not investing as much in the game.  I really like the campaign idea with choices you make one chapter carrying over to the next, but it's pretty obvious what is good to have (for example, the book says "If you get Maggie, it will help you in the future."), this turns into you just repeating a chapter until you get the good stuff, rather than being a case of choosing one of 2 or more equally promising paths and the suspense of seeing how your choice will play out in future chapters.  Lastly, we never really felt invested in our characters (unlike Dungeon Run, where we start to roleplay our characters). I am interested in seeing how the chapters play out, but not so interested in having to play through them. In the end, I am very happy I had a chance to play it before buying it - I will be passing on this.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Initial rating after 2 humiliating loses in the first chapter. I enjoy this game's difficulty. The first game was kind of rough with us rule checking and what not, but the second game flowed very smoothly. I feel if taught by an experienced player (like many adventure games) would be very easy to play. 

Maybe the best part was how intuitive everything was after you got into the flow of the gameplay. Roll your sword value to attack, shield value to defend. All you basically ever do is move and search otherwise. Cheese is good sometimes and bad others. What I really liked was the initiative track! It harkens back to Final Fantasy X's turn display, which is one of the real high points of that game. I love how it's dynamic (with characters sometimes shifting positions) and very clear (every stat and word you need for the enemy is right there). This game makes fantastic use of 'not too many' minis. There are only a handful but they variety in how they appear is clever, giving them a hint of personality, maybe my biggest complaint about WHQ, an orc is just an orc.

The problems I see are that it's literally mostly just rolling dice. There's not a lot of chance for clever tactics, the level up ability seems under powered once you have the 2 or 3 useful abilities your character can use (you start with 1). The design that allows 4 characters on one space is fresh, and the disengage rules good, often you just stand still and roll dice. I get that that's the core of this genre, but I think maybe they were too ambitious to have everything rolled on the same dice, versus having different dice rolled at different times.

While the game is generally of excellent quality, a couple component complaints I have are a lack of player aids (come on, what's this?), the number of dice included (ever play heroscape with 5 dice? more would be better) and the hero minis were constantly confused. I guess that encourages painting, and the minis look fantastic, but everyone moved the wrong piece multiple times.

RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A very thematic game. Theme ingrained even deeper by the amazing integration of the narrative in the game. 

Mechanically, the game is Descent Light; a narrative powered dungeon crawler, without loads of complex rules and a lot of visual aides to remind yourself about your character, their skills and equipment and several other mechanics like Initiative. 

A straight A+ recommendation for those looking for a way to make their little ones enthusiastic towards board gaming, roleplaying and fantasy stories. Be sure to guide their first steps though. While 'Light', it's not easy without a supervisor. ;)

For the more experienced dungeon crawlers among us this game might be a bit too 'Light' on the rules and options, and some mechanics definitely lack structure or balance.  ;) If you're looking for a game to crunch, look elsewhere.

This is a game that allows for a very cinematic experience. Personally one of my favourite games in the genre. It delivers what it promises, and does so in the best way possible.

High rating is based on the fact that this game delivers what it promises; a quick to learn, fun to play game to use as a gateway game with your children. For the parents? It's fun to go through this experience with your kids, but I'm already looking forward to introduce them to the more difficult Andor.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Every time I play this, it feels like I'm spending more time looking up rules than actually playing the game.
Also the game has some "gamey" rules that suck, like:
- loosing the currently equipped items when being captured, except those in the bag
- the need to roll a die to check if a mouse can leave water (yay, we lost because we all drowned!)
- the random initiative order (e.g. all enemies act before you in a boss encounter = instant death, vs. cakewalk vice versa)
- The mice "level up" and gain some (mostly useless) abilities, but they can't keep all their loot (why??)
- If mice are captured they cannot return before all enemies are defeated (seems overly punishing)

Other things that bothered us:
The number of player characters for each scenario is always given, no matter how many players there are. Having to control 2 (or even 3) characters at once distracts from the theme in this game and made us care less about the fate of the mice.

What's more, this game is a dice fest. Normally we are not bothered by prevalence of dice in a game, but here even movement is decided by dice. There are almost no meaningful decisions at all to be made.

The story aspect of this game is great but the game's mechanics, the gameplay and the rulebook are flawed.

RATING: N/A
The game is enjoyable, although I think it is best suited for kids.  It has an alright story I guess, although it is kind of silly at times.  The game can be fun to move through with friends.

The downside is the luck.  There is a LOT of dice rolling involved in this game.  So you have a lot of luck involved in this game for whether you are going to win.  One bad roll can sometimes completely knock your character out and you will be scrambling to recover.  On the other hand a good roll in that same situation and you might walk through the mission thinking it was a joke.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7

RATING: 5
There was a time when I thought this was a good game. I bought it following my friend's PhD viva, he was devastated with the result (major corrections within 12 months) and I wanted to take his mind off it. 

I started playing this game with his 3 daughters (one was always only observing and rolling the dice for her dad). After getting close to the end of the campaign, I stopped enjoying the game and so did the girls. What went wrong? Well, first of all the rules are a mess and don't lend themselves to a smooth gameplay. A few corner cases in a game are fine, but once every action becomes a corner case (can you attack enemies when you're in water? can enemies attack you when you're in water? these are 2 of hundreds of questions we had no answer to during the game) it becomes very annoying. Then there are the scenarios which are very unbalanced. The first scenario is a lot harder then the next 5 scenarios. What the hell? If this game is intended for younger players, the first mission is a terrible way to introduce them to the story. 

The characters are also imbalanced and it shows. It broke my heart to see one of the girls who picked Filch as her character at the start of the campaign come to realise she won't be as much help to the team as her sister who played the prince, simply because her character was much weaker. I picked this game to have fun with my friend and his kids, not to watch their enthusiasm die in front of my eyes.

But still, we pushed on. We persevered, we conquered, we reached one of the later scenarios (9, I think). It was in that scenario that the game informed us that it lied about the number of players on box, since only 2 players could play now. What the actual fsck? Here we were, all amped up and ready to play when the reality hit us in the face: only 2 of us were here to have fun, the rest could just sit and observe. Why? What was the point? Other than a small tidbit in the story, there was no reason for that. 

This is what tipped the scale. I could see everyone being less and less interested in the game as we progressed, but this extremely annoying experience is what pushed me to pull the plug. 

I think this game should not have been released in the current state. I think someone in the playtesting department (I assume there was one) dropped the ball in a major way here. This game could have a been a hit. It had all that was needed: interesting story, nice minis (which I painted to the delight of my friend's daughters) and fantastic-looking art. However, the gameplay just doesn't match the quality of the components. The game started as a 9/10 when I got it, dropped to 8 after the first session, then reached 6 by the 2-player only chapter. Now, half a year later, I think 5 is the most is deserves. Beautiful on the outside, but really ugly under the hood.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

One of my worst gaming decisions was to trade this away for a subpar game.  I had a difficult time getting this to the table, but that was more a problem with my typical gaming partners than with the game itself.

RATING: 5
[i]Too many dice rolls bog this charming game down. Not really any decisions to make, either.[/i]

Cool setting and gorgeous artwork. Seems a bit unpolished in some areas, and there is a bit too much dice rolling I think -- yeah, it's a dungeon crawl, of course there are a lot of dice! Problem here though is that you're often rolling the exact same dice repeatedly, since the bad guy is controlled by "AI", humans roll dice for his moves as well... and the same players rolling the same dice repeatedly gets repetitive.

Wonder if it would have been better off without defense rolls, as they slow down the pace of the game. Although the liklihood of your good attack roll being blocked can prolong the tension in a combat, since combat is 90% of the game (cannot progress until killing all minions in a tile) there isn't much build up or release of said tension so it is largely lost on me.

Pros: Great atmosphere, beautiful artwork, etc.

Cons: Repetitive and some of the mechanics can feel a little frustrating at times. Moreso than its competition, this one really does mostly just come down to dice I think. Dice game fueled by a story. There just aren't many decision points that aren't extremely obvious. No matter which class you play, you're pretty much just hacking and slashing, not being clever.

May grow on me more as we play through the Chapters, maybe some really cool stuff is done later on. Or if it goes down well with the niece and nephew. I think 4 player with adults + kids will be this game's sweet spot.

[hr]Played 10+ times now, and still wish this were more tactical (I'd rate it as less tactical even than the old school dungeon crawlers that it is inspired by)

(2 Design + 3 Enjoyment)

RATING: 4
Lack of player agenda. Winning or losing a scenario depends on luck at least as much as on group tactics, Limited enemy variety (and almost all of them just rush at you then dice fest until someone dies).

Outside combat (movement, loot search), failing die rolls just means wasting turns at the risk of running out of time and failing to complete the chapter in time.

Campaign mode too limited (skills maxed out after 2-3 chapters, impossibility of carrying much loot from one chapter to the next). In spite of the nominally different objectives, chapters mostly play the same way.

Redeeming qualities are production values and interesting story (esp. with children, although mine eventually got bored by chapter 5).

RATING: 3
1 play, 4er

This is a pretty straightforward dungeon-crawl type of game: you set up a scenario, start in a room with monsters, fight and kill them, search for items, and make progress through the map until you fulfill the scenario objective (in our case, we needed to get through 6 double-sided map tiles). If the game timer, which advances with random events and whenever a player gets knocked out, reaches the designated end everyone loses. It's all that, with:
- some interesting mechanics for ensuring each run-through is different (encounter cards, randomly chosen, dictate different monsters in different orders)
- simple but effective monster movement rules (attack closest person, but not if they've been attacked previously this combat)
- a stupid theme I don't care about (we're mice? really?)
- a lot of dice rolling, but you're often only rolling 1 or 2 dice so it feels VERY random
- minimal character advancement: the leveling up seems overly costly (hard to tell after one play, of course)

I was very glad when, after 84 minutes, we lost and could put this thing away! I can see that this could be much more fun with a younger audience but I would MUCH rather play Descent.

RATING: 7
Love dungeon crawlers but my wife hates complicated games... so I thought I'd give this a try. It took several chapters for me to get into this, but my wife loves it so we kept playing. It really comes alive in later chapters and is a lot of fun to play. It would be great with kids.

As a "dungeon crawlers" it really meets the demand for a "kill everything in the room before it kills you" fix. The downside is that there isn't a whole lot more tactical depth than that. Most tiles are big open rooms with little or no advantage to moving anywhere but towards your enemies. Ranged attacks hit everything in line of sight, which is usually everywhere, and the tiles are so small it seems you are never too far away from anything to be safe. But all that makes it simple and easy to learn and good for people that don't want a 40 page rule book and tacklebox full of bits. (I have Descent 2ed so I'm already fixed there!)
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I really wanted to love this game, but it's just too random. It has a great premise, simple mechanics, engaging story, and gorgeous art, but it is a frustrating experience as a cooperative game. The reason for this is that it's too easy to be defeated by rolling too much cheese for the minions and some of the minor minions are just too hard. It's easy to get overwhelmed by too many enemies (at times we have had to use counters because we ran out of miniatures). And death is just too harsh. All of these things could probably be forgiven if it had a grittier theme, but it positively screams "kid's game" with its simple rules and storybook theme, but your kids are likely to scream after they've been bested by bad dice rolling for the fourth game in a row on the same scenario. Tremendous potential, but it just doesn't deliver.

RATING: 7
Rating based only on playing the first adventure.  The theme is very strong and the rules are fairly easy to understand without sacrificing too much game play. RATING: 6.5
I think Mice and Mystics story narrative is very well done. I am only on chapter 3 so I can't comment on replayability until I have done all of the chapters. I like the initiative track and although it's combat system is not very deep I do like it better than the D&D games. I like to position my mice and I like being able to roll some dice for defense (vs being at the mercy of a d20).

I would like greater variety in bad guys.

I like the leveling up options here as well.

Looking forward to seeing what the next chapters hold. 

Update: During our 5th play both kids wanted to stop before finishing. My 11 year old son grew tired of the over all length of the game and the amount of down time between turns. He also wasn't enamored with his choices/results during his turn (a lot of his Filch attacks were blocked). My 5 year old daughter is still willing to play but it ran too long for her as well.

I know I could just play part of a chapter, but that feels unsatisfying and we don't have table space to keep the game up for an extended time.

My son actually said he would rather play Candy Land. Candy Land is probably his least favorite game too. He just wanted the game to end quickly.

I really enjoy playing games solo, but oddly enough I don't feel like giving this a go on my own. Not when I have Thunderbolt Apache Leader and Lord of the Rings:LCG.

We'll see what happens the next time we play (without my son).

We tried it a few more times and the kids reached the conclusion (well my daughter at least) that she didn't want to play the game anymore...she just wanted to hear how the story turns out.  So, I read the chapters to her and put the game up for trade.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Lovely components. The miniatures look fantastic, and will be good for a new painter or a veteran. Tiles are thick, art is great.
The overall mechanics work well; exploring and moving around the castle is smooth, and the 'flip' mechanic allowing you to travel through the floor and ceiling is very clever and thematic. Combat is basic, but there are some interesting abilities and treasures. The cheese mechanic is a decent way to drive special powers.

Lots of complaints and nit-picks: There are only two female characters, and they are completely irrelevant to the plot. Lots of confusing spots in the scenarios; often we've had no idea how we are supposed to play situations. Most scenarios are 4 player, but one is only 2 1/2 and one is 3 1/2 (1/2 meaning "a player that doesn't work well or really participate"). Needs scenario reference cards for all the special rules in each room. Several party items have plenty of room for summaries of the item, but just don't bother. 1 more die would make die sharing a lot smoother. Low key advancement does mean you can drop characters in and out, but it also means there's not much feeling of progress. You can't keep enough items to make some abilities useful.

I don't feel any attachment or investment in the characters; they are clearly someone else's characters in someone else's story.

Overall, this seems like a game that's less than the sum of its parts. It's fun, but it's missing something - possibly a lot of somethings. I doubt we'll be going back to it after completing the campaign.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Hmm...bit undecided on this one. The gameplay is ok, but very basic. It's designed for family, younger kids etc. The problem is the scenarios go on for way to long. We are only on the early chapters, but we found even they can take hours to finish. 

The issue is the gameplay doesn't have the depth needed to support these lengthy play times. It becomes very repetitive and we found ourselves just wanting it to end at times.

Thematically, M&M is one the best games out there, but the lack of gameplay depth combined with the long playtime is what really brings the game down. 

I think this is a one and done. I really couldn't see myself wanting to play this through a 2nd time. I am actually surprised it's rated as highly as it is. It seems many people are so blinded by the great story and theme that they can't see the woods through the trees. 

It's a shame...it really is, I want to like this more. At the moment I rate it a 6, but I can easily see this dropping further with more plays.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A fun, light dungeon crawler with a novel setting, a fun story, a beautiful aesthetic, and plenty of great in-game thematic touches.  It seems like it would be a fantastic game for kids, though the rules are more complicated than something like HeroQuest (I need to reference the rulebook much more often than I'd like).

But I do think the game system relies too much on dice: combat, movement, searching for items, gaining "currency" (cheese), the game clock, getting out of water before washing away... EVERYTHING is based on die rolls.  One session could turn out to be quite easy and another time it could be a frustrating and futile endeavour, even if you made all the exact same choices each time.  Player agency takes a back seat while luck drives the bus, and sometimes that leads to a bumpy ride.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I have to give this a 9... no 10 for the scattered rules.  The characters are fantastic, the minis are really nice (plastic though, not resin), and the story is actually more involved than you might think at first, and honestly, should be considered by Pixar.  My suggestion, as well, is for one person to become very familiar with the rules before getting the family in on the fun.  Also, if you have someone who can really read stories (enthusiasm, voices), then this game will truly shine.

I have been running/playing games for about 40 years and the latest crop of rules are either great, or quite a mess.  This one isn't quite the latter but the rules are dense, the booklet is a page flipper, and there are a number of conditions and modifiers you should at least have an idea where to find in the book so as not to slow the game down.

With that accomplished, and the game on the table (expect a couple of nights JUST for the first chapter, especially if you have younger children), Mice and Mystics should become a favorite, and will tell a story that will leave an impression.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
[thing=124708][/thing] is a light game of mice heroism, exploring tunnels, sewers, dining rooms, kitchens and such places. A mice life isn't a safe one, because there are evil rats, big spiders, roaches - some of them greedy! - and terrible centipedes. But the kingdom must be rescued from the hands of the dark sorceress Vanestra, that put the King under her spell, and now the King lies in his bed, an inch from death. His loyal servants were arrested and, in jail, the wizard Maginos used a powerful conjuration to turn everyone in the cell into little mice, in order to escape. But, now they cannot turn back into human form! So, in their new mice might (cuteness?), they will try to do what everything that needs to be done to right the wrongs.

The theme in [thing=124708][/thing] is paramount to its enjoyment. It is a fairy tale, so expect fairy tale things - talking animals, weird magic, heroism even when facing overwhelmingly odds. There are long passages that are nothing more than flavor text, but, sure they are tasty ones.

The rules, inspite of the thematic pressure, are solid: more on the light side, but with enough depth to be interesting to gamers, young or not.

The replayability, normally an issue in most games with scenarios to be played, isn't in its higher form in here, but there is enough for a good lot of plays, because: you have more mice than you can use in a given mission; there is more special abilities that you can get; the Search uncover a plethora of items and events (you will probably won't see all of them even if you play the whole campaign); the enemies appear in a tile semi-randomly: it depends on the point of the Chapter that the story is; and, of course, because of the dice rolls - in a Chapter, one usually punny Rat can become a Rodent Demigod, resisting to everything and capturing everyone, for example.

The components are top notch and the art is climatic, really well done in every way. Our plays took us anywhere between 60 to 150 minutes.

[thing=124708][/thing] provides a good level of cooperation between players, because many of the skills of the mice work only if they are together (like Tilda's Mace) or work in the others (like many of the special skills from the Leader deck).

All in all, [thing=124708][/thing] provides a great experience and I'm sure will play the whole campaign, and the sooner, the better!

RATING: 6
Not my usual sort of game, but with kids it's fantastic. 

So a new favorite family fun game with wonderful thematic latching. A much improved co-op notion than Pandemic for this sort of table, as it's about an RPG-like creativity working together to get silly things done racing a ticking clock. Much less constraining than other co-ops. For example, the group gets to share it's stuff while taking on the roaches, spiders, cats, and environmental puzzles, unlike co-ops that make even sharing something a tempo laden puzzle to negotiate.

Lots of laughter, tension, and no bossiness.

RATING: 8
A rewarding Ameritrash co-op. This one must be a love child. Beautiful and thematic art, nice miniatures that couldn't resist to paint and good quality components (minus the cards which require sleeving, the typical fail of PHG -products) and engraved symbol dice. Yummy story connecting the scenarios and seems to work for quite a large age scale, some character development through skills and items (we want more!) and possibility to play a campaign. Co-op works well with two and four players while the three player game involves one player more (four mice divided between players). For anyone seeking to save the kingdom, free the righteous king from wicked enchantment and ready to go fearless against centipede, rats, doomsday machine and whatnot. Works as a family game for us.

RATING: 10
This is my absolute favorite boardgame currently. I love the Mouseguard/Redwall theme, and the engaging story element of the game. 

It is a dungeoncrawler with heart, and with characters that I really grew to care about as the story progressed.

This is also a great family game, and a good "gateway" game for children or reluctant spouses/significant others in my experience.

I have a soft spot as well for cooperative games, and this one definitely fits the bill, with all players taking on the role of the heroes. Unlike many games of this type, there is no player controlling the monsters, which adds an extra element of cooperation amongst all players. 

I can't reccommend this game any more highly, and I am looking forward to the upcoming (2) expansions!

RATING: 5
This is a well made game, and if you want a game with a deep story (maybe because you are playing with children), then I would recommend it.

My low rating is because it is not a game that I enjoy playing.  It focuses far too much on story, and not enough on interesting game play.  There is a little bit of luck mitigation (some bad die rolls provide cheese -- basically mana -- when they fail), but not nearly enough.  Roll well, and winning will be easy.  Roll poorly, and even the intro scenario will kill you.

RATING: 5
PLAYING WITH KIDS RATING:  [bgcolor=#99FFFF][s][color=#99FFFF]-[/color][/s][b]7[/b][s][color=#99FFFF]-[/color][/s][/bgcolor]

A kid-friendly dungeon crawler.  Game play is basic kill & level up which gets a bit repetitive after a few chapters, but the kids enjoy the story (reminiscent of the [url=https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mouse_Guard]Mouse Guard[/url] books) and focus more on building up their mouse character rather than advancing the group's aim.  The game and the campaign require a fair bit of overhead to go along with an unexpectedly steep learning curve for a game advertised as ages 7 and up.  Sure a seven year old can participate, but a bigger kid or an adult needs to do the heavy lifting of knowing the rules (at least initially) and keeping the game machine running.  The rulebook covers all the bases, but it could have been laid out better and/or had a better index.  Co-op's and dungeon crawlers are not among my favorites and this game further entrenches that sentiment.  A fun way to spend some time with the kids, but after the halfway mark of the campaign my eldest (10) has lost some enthusiasm.  My youngest (7) still very much enjoys the game.  Will likely take an extended break after the campaign before we start on the already acquired expansion.

RATING: 7
A game that missed by a seven years because my kids are now too old to appreciate it.  Rating is for families with fantasy-loving children and adults that are barely in touch with reality. Like me.

Mice and Mystics could teach a lesson to the Descent family, since tying random monster spawns to the story progression is a smart innovation - though it can lead to high-speed losing if too many cheese symbols appear.

The initiative track hijinks (e.g., the Rat's special ability) is another example of a clever twist on standard dungeon crawlers.

Would play again, this time with D-Con.

RATING: 7
This is a unique offering in the dungeon crawl class.  Highest appeal is for kids, but would also appeal greatly to those adults turned off by the normal "hack-n'-slash" theme of dungeon crawls.  The game is thematically much more rich than others of its ilk.  The story-line parts add a really nice element, especially for kids, but adults should not find them too "cheesy."  I found play very smooth and the rules straightforward, if you do not try to over-interpret them but instead just focus on what they allow.  My only qualm is that it gets kind of samey after a while, but really this is a problem with all dungeon crawl types.  The advantage with this game is that they can release new story books with no or minimal components and make reasonably priced expansions, vs. the mega-costly-stuffed boxes you get from something like FFG's Descent.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5
'Mice and Mystics' is a cute, charismatic game with a very evocative narrative and graphic design. This really is a game I would like to play with kids who could get really get into the theme of rodent warriors fighting against an army of vermin. 

For me personally, though, I think the gameplay is too shallow and repetitive. You do the same thing over and over again: move, fight, roll dice. Rinse and repeat. And the game may have an amazing story, if the gameplay isn't there to back it up, I'm simply not interested. The dice rolling is really lucky. For about 2/3 of the game I wasn't able to hit ANYTHING with Maginos (the mage mouse), only to wipe out THREE(!) rats toward the end of the game in one blow. Moments like that are great, but they can be few and far between. 

So ultimately, I would recommend this as a kid's dungeoncrawl adventure story before bedtime, but one more advanced, serious gamers can easily steer away from.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
I simply do not understand the ratings for this game unless you are solely playing it with your pre-teen daughter who likes the cute theme.  If you completely ignore the theme, this is simply a very boring dungeon crawl without almost any decisions beyond move and attack.  Yeah, there is a bit of a story, but so many other games do it better.  I can't see any reason why adults would want to play this amongst themselves.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
I have pretty mixed feelings about this game and my rating adequately reflects this.

This game can definitely drag for a player that isn't so lucky at rolling dice.  Not only did I experience this personally, but so did others in my group.  Since much of the combat, movement, defense and searches rely solely on successful dice rolls, it becomes immediately apparent why luck is critical to enjoy this game.  To be quite honest, I was quite frustrated losing my first two games only because of poor dice rolls, and NOT a result of bad strategy or any lack of understanding of the game rules.  In my opinion, this is a MAJOR flaw that this game embodies.

There are times when characters in the game definitely feel some downtime and there are no fulfilling actions available for that character other than to search.  Unfortunately, even this is limited as a character can only search a tile once successfully.  Also, the initiative track prevents players from strategizing effectively to determine the best turn order for the group.  
 
The components in this game are excellent!  I give Plaid Hat Games two thumbs up on the production value.  My only gripe of any of the components are the terribly organized and incomplete rule and scenario books.

Where this game fully shines is in the extremely creative narratives that carry the players through a series of quests, so to speak!  I found this aspect quite unique in that I actually feel as if I am reading a story of these mice and their adventures.  As one can note by the ratings found here on BGG for this game, it has become many people's favorite game in such a short amount of time; thus, ending up in a geek's top 10 list.

It is definitely not one of my favorite games, but I am happy to have it in my collection.  It will not see the table as much as others due to its luck dependence and fiddly rules, but it could be a great gateway game to introduce others to the hobby, especially younger players.

-Final Thoughts-
It is extremely apparent that the majority of high ratings are those who play this game with a much younger player (son, daughter, nephew, niece...).  Otherwise, this game seems to be relatively mediocre in a roll-move-roll-battle... rinse and repeat fashion.  It is obvious that the designer of this game was not consistent with his choice of game audience as M&M feels all over the place, which leads to an unstructured and minimally fulfilling experience for the adult gamer.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

tip: to get you in the right mood, read the Depthford Mice trilogy from Robin Jarvis and the Mouse Guard comics by David Petersen.

RATING: 8
My only real complaint is how luck/dice dependent this is. If there were some other options for (useful) actions, it'd be a 10 in my book.
Otherwise, the characters are colorful and the story is engaging. Best played with 2, maybe 3, players. Components are of exceptional quality, imo. I have half a mind to get my miniatures painted!

RATING: 10
My wife and I enjoyed playing through the campaign so, so much. Even if it's not quite as enjoyable to replay the chapters this game was still worth  the price just for the first set of play-throughs. This game might not be perfect, but it was absolutely perfect for us, and that's why it gets a 10.

RATING: 10
The theme, the artwork, the story! What a wonderful game! Combat is surprisingly deep once the mice heroes have obtained some extra abilities. Cannot wait for future expansions!

My review of Mice & Mystics compared to another favourite of mine, Legend of Drizzt, can be read here:
